+Jamison Brereton

54 (288)
All Gods
Praj─Бpati Vai┼Ыv─Бmitra or Praj─Бpati V─Бcya
22 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This first hymn to the All Gods in this maс╣Зс╕Нala is something of a hybrid, combining two standard approaches to All God hymns. On the one hand, the second half of the hymn (starting with vs. 11) treats these deities as a list, granting a verse each to a number of gods and mentioning their familiar characteristics. This part is relatively straightforward.
The first half, especially verses 2тАУ9, is ostensibly devoted to Heaven and Earth, but, though it begins as a conventional praise of those paired deities, as often in All God hymns the divinity provides a point of departure for spec ulation on the nature of things and unanswered questions about cosmic mat ters; see especially the questions in verse 5, at the middle of this self-contained hymn-within-a-hymn. The emphasis on truth and reality and on the discovery of Heaven and Earth (for both themes see vss. 3тАУ4), in combination with the uncer tain questions, suggests that the point is that we only gradually and imperfectly discover the real dimensions and nature of the cosmos. The style in this portion is enigmatic, intense, and rhetorically intricate, especially in the climactic verse 9, where Heaven as the divine begetter, and perhaps the single principle, and heaven as a place, the home of the gods to which we also aspire, seem to be referred to simultaneously. This double reference is aided by the ambiguity of the first verb in the verse, ├бdhy emi, which can mean either тАЬI go uponтАЭ or тАЬI study.тАЭ Verse 10 clearly closes off that part of the hymn and makes the transition to the second part and its list of favored gods.
The hymn begins with a verse to Agni and ends with a verse and a half to him, thus providing a larger ring around the two very different halves.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬThey recite repeatedly this gratifying praise to the great product of sacrifice (Agni); may he who is (endowed) with domestic radiance hear us; may the imperishable Agni, (endowed) with divine radiance, hear us.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

This fortifying (hymn) here have they presented to the great one
belonging to the rite, who is to be reverently invoked repeatedly time after time.
Let him listen to us with his faces belonging to the house; let
inexhaustible Agni listen with (his faces) belonging to heaven.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬKnowing their greatness, offer worship to the vast heaven and to the earth; my desire, wishing (for felicity) proceed (to them), in whose praise the gods,desirous of adoration, delight together with their worshippers at the sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

My desire proceeds: k─Бma me icchan carati = liс╣н, my desire wishing goes, or exists; added to icchan, sarv─Бn bhog─Бn, all enjoyments

+Jamison Brereton

I will recite a great (hymn) to great Heaven and to Earth. My desire, seeking, knowing the way, goes (to those two),
at the praise of whom the gods, seeking service at the rites, become
exhilarated in company with them.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) I supply тАЬto those twoтАЭ in b, to provide both a goal for ich├б├▒ carati and an antecedent for y├бyoс╕е in c.

III.54.3-4: The co-occurrence of с╣Ыt├б- and saty├б- in these two vss. (3a, 4b) is striking.

In keeping with my estimation of the difference in meaning between the two, I tr. the first as тАШtruthтАЩ and the latter as тАШreal(ity)тАЩ. In both cases here the sense of saty├б- is close to the English idiom тАЬcome true,тАЭ that is, тАЬbecome real.тАЭ In 3a the poet is asking that the cosmic truth(s) associated with Heaven and Earth be realized in our own sphere, that H+E put themselves out, as it were, for our benefit. 4ab also concerns the truth(s) associated with H+E – hence the adj. с╣Ы╠Бt─Бvar─л тАШtruthfulтАЩ – and the older poets, in finding these two entities that possess their own truth(s), spoke words (presumably about and in praise of H+E) that both reflected the reality of those truths and that also came true (satyav─Б╠Бcaс╕е). This vs. esp. emphasizes the poetsтАЩ process of discovery of the truths about H+E.

As Renou points out, the vs. contrasts the priests or poets in ab with the warriors in cd.

+Griffith

To mighty Heaven and Earth I sing forth loudly: my wish goes out desirous and well knowing
Both, at whose laud in synods, showing favour, the Gods rejoice them with the living mortal.

+Geldner

Ein hohes Lied will ich dem hohen Himmel, der Erde singen. Mein Wunsch geht suchend, den Weg kennend zu ihnen, an deren beider Loblied bei den Opfern die G├╢tter voll Ergebenheit zusammen mit ihnen sich erg├╢tzen.

+Grassmann

Laut sing’ der Erd’ ich und dem grossen Himmel, begehrend geht mein Wunsch, des Weges kundig, Bei ihrem Preise freuen sich die G├╢tter, die treuen bei den Festen mit den beiden.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHeaven and earth, may your truth be ever inviolable; be propitious to us for the due completion of the rite; this adoration (Agni) is offered to heaven and earth; I worship (them) with (sacrificial) food; I solicit of them precious (wealth).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let your truth be real, you two world-halves. Come to the fore for our great welfare.
Here is homage to Heaven and to Earth, o Agni. I render service with a pleasurable offering; I beg for a treasure.

+Griffith

O Heaven and Earth, may your great law he faithful: he ye our leaders for our high advantage.
To Heaven and Earth I offer this my homage, with food, O Agni, as I pray for riches.

+Geldner

Euer Gesetz soll die Wahrheit sein, Himmel und Erde! Tretet fein f├╝r unser gro├Яes Wohlergehen ein! Diese Verbeugung gilt dem Himmel, der Erde, o Agni. Ich warte mit einem Labsal auf; ich bitte um Belohnung.

+Grassmann

Euch, Welten beide, sei das Opfer wirksam, zu grossem Wohlstand m├╢gt ihr uns voran gehn; Dem Himmel weih’ ich dies Gebet, der Erde, durch Opferspeise komme ich zu Reichthum.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHeaven and earth, endowed with truth, they who are the ancient declarers of the truth, have obtained from you (what they desired); and so, earth, men cognizant (of the greaness of you both) have worshipped you for the sake of triumphing over (hostile) heroes in battle.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

For also the ancient ones, speaking what is real, found you two, you truthful world-halves.
Also the superior men at the clash, at the contest of champions, extolled you two, o (Heaven and) Earth, as they kept discovering you.

+Griffith

Yea, holy Heaven and Earth, the ancient sages whose word was ever true had power to find you;
And brave men in the fightwhere heroes conquer, O Earth, have known you well and paid you honour.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWho knows what is the truth, or who may here declare it? What is the proper path that leads to the gods? Their inferior abiding plural ces are beheld, as are those which (are situated) in superior mysterious rites.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abiding plural ces are beheld: as the constellations; superior mysterious rites: in the latter they are made known, it is said, by the Veda

+Jamison Brereton

Who knows for certain? Who will here proclaim (it)? What is the pathway that leads to the gods?
Their lowest seats are visible, (but those) that are amid the highest
hidden commandments… ?

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda is also found in the famous cosmogonic (or anti-cosmogonic) hymn X.129, as 6a. The final p─Бda of that hymn, X.129.7d, ends with an incomplete sentence тАЬor if he does not know тАж?тАЭ (y├бdi v─Б n├б v├йda). Though all the standard tr.

of this vs. here find a way to incorporate our 5d into the syntax of the verse, I by contrast think the same trailing off into uncertainty is found here as in X.129.7. The lower seats of the gods in heaven can be seen, but not the ones in the higher realms.

We can only discover so much. As for grammar, I take the y─Б╠Бof d as a neut. pl.

referring to s├бd─Бс╣Гsi in c (so also Renou, though with a slightly different interpr. of the rest). Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) instead take it as a fem. nom. sg. referring to the pathy─Б╠Аin b, with c as parenthetical. I do not entirely understand the vrat├йс╣гu in d. The hidden commandments may be the laws that govern the further reaches of the cosmos.

+Griffith

Seen are their lowest dwelling-places only, but they are in remote and secret regions.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe far-seeing beholder of mankind (the sun), surveys this heaven and earth, rejoicing when deficient in moisture in the womb of the waters (the firmament), both concurring in community (of function), although they occupy various dwellings, like the diversified nests of a bird.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In community of function: in the interchange of moisture

+Jamison Brereton

The sage poet, (though) having a manтАЩs sight, has looked upon them: the two [=Heaven and Earth], separated but becoming exhilarated
(together) in the womb of truth.
The two have made a seat each for herself as a bird does, (though) being united by a joint purpose.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the somewhat anomalous use of nс╣Ыc├бkс╣гas- here see comm. ad III.53.9.

The first p─Бda of this vs. seems to imply that, though the higher seats of the gods are not generally visible (5d), a kav├н-, despite having only a manтАЩs sight, has been able to see (abh├н тАж acaс╣гс╣нa) Heaven and Earth whole, and that he is cognizant of the crucial paradox about them — that they are joined but still distinct – a paradox treated in the rest of the vs. and the following one (7).

The interpr. of b is hampered by the hapax v├нghс╣Ыte. On the surface it appears to belong to the root тИЪghс╣Ы тАШsprinkleтАЩ, but it is difficult to make this yield immediate sense. It appears to serve the same function as v├нyute тАШseparatedтАЩ in the next vs. (7a), and it has therefore been suggested that -ghс╣Ыta- actually belong to the root тИЪhс╣Ы тАШtakeтАЩ or is a byform thereof (see, e.g., KEWA III.578). My published translation reflects a tacit acceptance of such a view (or at least a willingness not to probe it too deeply), but I now wonder (without full conviction) whether in the context of m├бdant─л тАШbecoming exhilaratedтАЩ a sense that connects v├нghс╣Ыte to тИЪghс╣Ы тАШsprinkleтАЩ might be possible: тАЬsprinkled separately but becoming exhilarated (together).тАЭ In any event I take it as a dual fem. acc. (with Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н]), not, with Renou, a loc. sg. with y├│n─Б.

My tr. also depends on assuming that the exhilarating is happening jointly, in contrast to whatever type of separation is indicated by the v├н-prefixed ppl. – the same contrast between unity and separation found in cd. The place where this is happening in b, тАЬthe womb of truthтАЭ (с╣Ыt├бsya y├│n─Б), may refer to two different places, the ritual ground (as so often) and, perhaps, the distant invisible seats referred to in 5d.

+Griffith

The Sage who looketh on mankind hath viewed them bedewed, rejoicing in the seat of Order.
They make a home as for a bird, though parted, with one same will finding themselves together.

+Geldner

Der Seher mit dem Herrenauge hat sie erschaut, die gesondert im Scho├Яe des Gesetzes schwelgen. An getrennten Orten haben sie ihren Sitz bereitet wie der Vogel und sind doch eintr├дchtig in gleichem Geiste.

+Grassmann

Sie schaute an der m├дnnerschau’nde Seher, die seligen, im heil’gen Schooss besprengten; Beseelt von gleichem Geiste machten beide verschieden ihren Sitz, wie den des Vogels.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬCommon (in function), disjoined, of distant termination, they remain vigilant in a permanent station; being, as it were, sisters, and ever young; they therefore address each other by twin appellations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Heaven and earth are the person nifications here alluded to; address each other by twin appellations: ─Бdu bruv─Бte mithun─Бni n─Бma; heaven and earth are designated together by urvi and other duplicate terms: urvy─Бdibhir dvandva n─Бm─Бbhir dy─Бv─Бpс╣Ыthivyavucyate

+Jamison Brereton

Jointly but kept apart, with their ends at a distance, they have taken their stand in a fixed place, wakeful.
And (though) they are sisters and young women, they are called
opposing names.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The -┼л╠Бka-stem j─Бgar┼л╠Бka- in b is found only here in Vedic. I wonder if it owes its -ka-suffix to the femininized context of c, where H+E are identified as тАЬsisters and young womenтАЭ (sv├бs─Бr─Б yuvat─л╠Б) despite their oppositely gendered names.

On -ka- in womenтАЩs language, see my тАЬWomenтАЩs Language in the Rig Veda?тАЭ (Gd.

Elizarenkova, 2008) and тАЬSociolinguistic Remarks on the Indo-Iranian *-ka-Suffix: A Marker of Colloquial RegisterтАЭ (IIJ 53 [2009]).

Note the virtual mirror image of v├нyute (a) and yuvat─л╠Б(c).

I do not understand the use of ─Б╠Бd u here. Ordinarily this old ablative has a fairly strong temporal (тАЬjust after thatтАЭ) or logical (тАЬbecause of thatтАЭ) sense, but since c has a concessive force (тАЬalthough being тАжтАЭ), it is difficult to get ─Б╠Бd to have logical force, and the fact of being sisters but called different names does not seem to have a temporal dimension. It reminds of the ca тАж ─Б╠Бd in 11cd, but there ─Б╠Бd easily expresses a standard temporal sense. It is possible, but extremely speculative, that the ─Б╠Бd does reflect some sort of cosmic temporality: H+E, originally joined together, had a single identity and gender, but after the cosmogonic separation they received different, and genderedly oppositional, names. The monism of the next vs. (8cd) might (barely) support such an idea; note that тАЬthe OneтАЭ there is neut. (├йkam).

The standard interpr. (see Geldner, etc.) of mithun─Б╠Бni n─Б╠Бma is that their names are of different genders when they are given separate names, with dya├║с╕е generally masc.

and pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бfem. But they are also paired sisters, with the fem. du. designation r├│das─л.

This seems correct, and the published translation should probably have reflected this sense of mithun├б- better. I am somewhat puzzled by why the names are in the plural, however.

+Griffith

Partners though parted, with far-distant limits, on one firm place both stand for ever watchful,
And, being young for evermore, as sisters, speak to each other names that are united.

+Geldner

In gleicher Weise und doch getrennt stehen die beiden fern endenden auf fester Grundlage immer wachsam. Zwar sind die Jugendlichen Schwestern, doch f├╝hren sie paarweise m├дnnlichen und weiblichen Namen.

+Grassmann

Gemeinsam und getrennt doch, unermesslich, an festem Orte standen beide wachsam; Und als zwei Schwestern immer jung verbleibend, verk├╝nden nun sie ihre Zwillingsnamen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThese two keep all born things discrete, and, although comprehending the great divinities, are not distressed; all moving and stationary beings rest upon one (basis), whether animals, or birds, or creatures of various kinds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Keep all born things discrete: heaven and earth all that is born distinct, by furnishing interval or space, avak─Б┼Ыaprad─Бnena

+Jamison Brereton

All these races do the two contain. (Though) supporting the great gods, they do not waver.
The One is master of all: the moving and the fixed, the walking and the flying, of various sorts, variously born.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The notion of the pair of H+E, separate but unified, is, in the 2nd hemistich, replaced by an even starker contrast, the One (├йkam, neut. as noted in comm. to previous vs.), which controls the Many, with the Many first configured as oppositional pairs in the neuter: the moving and the fixed (├йjad dhruv├бm), the walking/roaming and the flying (c├бrad patatr├н). ├йkam is found at the end of its p─Бda, just as it is in the refrain to the next hymn (III.55).

+Griffith

All living things they part and keep asunder; though bearing up the mighty Gods they reel not.
One All is Lord of what is fixed and moving, that walks, that flies, this multiform creation.

+Geldner

Diese beiden fassen alle Gesch├╢pfe in sich; sie tragen die gro├Яen G├╢tter und kommen doch nicht ins Wanken. Das Eine beherrscht alles was sich regt und was fest ist, was geht und was fliegt, das Verschiedenartige, verschieden Geborene.

+Grassmann

Sie halten alle Wesen auseinander, sie wanken nicht, die grossen G├╢tter tragend; Bewegtes, festes, alles hegt die eine, was geht und fliegt, das mannichfach geborne.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI consider at present the eternal and ancient sisterhood to us of you, our great protectress and progenitrix, within whose vast and separated path your eulogists, the gods, travel in their chariots.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Protectress and progenitrix: mahaс╕е pitur janitur j─Бmi tan naс╕е = mahatyaс╕е p─Бlayitryaс╕е janayitryastava, of you, that is, of the heaven;

J─Бmi = j─Бmitva, or bhaginitvam, sisterhood, the condition of a relative sister; this will not allow of pit─Б and janit─Б being rendered father and progenitor

+Jamison Brereton

From afar I tread upon the ancient (path) of old [/study the ancient One of old]: that is our relationship to the great father [=Heaven?], the begetter, where [=in heaven?] the gods, as admirers, in their own ways took their stand within (it) on their (own) broad separate path.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the meaning of this vs. see published introduction. It is the final vs. of the hymnwithin-the hymn, vss. 2-9 dedicated to Heaven and Earth. The 1st ps. poet reappears here; he is first found in vs. 2, the beginning of this self-contained portion, and has been absent since, though he may be related to the 3rd ps. kav├н- in vs. 6.

As indicated in the published introduction, I think this vs. has a double meaning, aided by the double readings of two items in it: ├бdhi тИЪi, which means both тАШgo uponтАЩ (literally) and тАШstudyтАЩ (тАШgo overтАЩ, figuratively), and the unnamed dya├║с╕е, present both as the divinity Heaven alluded to in the phrase in b тАЬgreat father, begetterтАЭ (gen. mah├бс╕е pit├║r janit├║с╕е; for this as a designation of dya├║с╕е cf., e.g., I.164.33 dya├║r me pit─Б╠Бjanit─Б╠Б) and as heaven the place, suggested by the locational adv. y├бtra тАШwhereтАЩ in c, introducing the place where the gods take their stand. The poet is both studying the ancient cosmic mysteries he has been attempting to understand in the previous vss.

(esp. 5-6) and is embarking on the path that leads to the place where the gods are established, beyond the ken of mortals. Recall the question in 5b тАЬWhat is the pathway that leads to the gods?тАЭ (dev─Б╠Бm╠Р├бch─Б pathy─Б╠Аk─Б╠Бs├бm eti), a question followed by the statement that only the lower seats of the gods are visible. Here pur─Бс╣З├бm in p─Бda a can qualify тАШpathтАЩ – not the fem. pathy─Б╠Аin 5b but the more familiar masc.

p├бnth─Б-, qualified as pur─Бс╣З├б- in IV.18.1 (cf. also pur─Бс╣З├бm ├│kaс╕е тАШancient homeтАЩ in nearby III.58.6, referring to the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ dwelling, presumably also heaven). The gods are themselves on a separate path (path├н vy├╣te d) in the same place, at least by my interpr. Despite their different representations in the (written) Saс╣Гhit─Б text and in the Pp., vy├╣ta- here and v├нyuta- in 7a must be the same form, ppl. to v├н тИЪyu; in recitation they would be identical. The verb unoti to the supposed root тИЪu to which vy├╣ta- is sometimes referred (see, e.g., Geldner n. 9d) is actually also a form of тИЪyu, in the sequence vy├╣noti in V.31.1, also meaning тАШseparatesтАЩ. Cf. EWA II.503.

+Griffith

Afar the Ancient from of old I ponder, our kinship with our mighty Sire and Father,-
Singing the praise whereof the Gods by custom stand on the spacious far-extended pathway.

+Geldner

Von Ferne erkenne ich das Uralte: Das ist unsere Abstammung von dem gro├Яen Vater, dem Erzeuger, auf dem Weg zu dem die G├╢tter eifrig Beifall spendend auf ihrem weiten, abgesonderten Wege dazwischen treten.

+Grassmann

Das alte stets erw├дg’ ich aus der Ferne, dies unser Stammen von dem grossen Vater, Wo anerkennend, wie gewohnt, die G├╢tter auf den gebahnten breiten Pfaden standen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI repeat this hymn, heaven and earth, to you; and may the soft-bellied, fire-tongued Mitra, royal Varuс╣Зa, the youthful ─Аdityas, all cognizant of the past, and proclaiming (their own acts), hear it.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Proclaiming: paprath─Бn─Бс╕е = sv─Бni sv─Бni karm─Бс╣Зi prathayantaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

This praise here I proclaim, you two world-halves. The tender-hearted ones having Agni as their tongue will hear itтАФ
the youthful sovereign kings, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, the ─Аdityas, sage poets, extending far and wide.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. forms a sort of ring with vs. 1, enclosing the Heaven and Earth hymnlet of vss. 2-9. Like vs. 1 it begins with im├бm followed by a word for hymn (1a im├бm тАж ┼Ы┼лс╣г├бm, 10a im├бс╣Г st├│mam), and with 1cd it contains a verb form of тИЪ┼Ыru тАШhearтАЩ with god(s) as subject (10b).

On с╣Ыd┼лd├бra- see EWA s.v. ARD, though he is somewhat cagey about its formation. I assume the 2nd member is ud├бra- тАШbellyтАЩ, with the literal sense тАШmoistbelliedтАЩ being equivalent to our тАШtender-heartedтАЩ. This assumes a bahuvr─лhi with an adjectival first member of the form с╣Ыdu-, a shape (disyllabic adj. ending in -i- or -u-) that often triggers (or is at least associated with) 2nd member accent in bahuvr─лhis (see AiG II.1.296ff.).

+Griffith

This laud, O Heaven and Earth, to you I utter: let the kind-hearted hear, whose tongue is Agni,
Young, Sovran Rulers, Varuna and Mitra, the wise and very glorious Adityas.

+Geldner

Dieses Loblied trage ich vor, ihr Rodasi. Die weichherzigen G├╢tter sollen es h├╢ren, deren Zunge Agni ist, die jugendlichen Allk├╢nige Mitra, Varuna, die Aditya┬┤s, die weit und breit bekannten Seher.

+Grassmann

Euch sprech’ ich aus, o Welten, dieses Loblied, die feuerzung’nen, holden, m├╢gen h├╢ren, Die jungen weisen Varuna und Mitra, die weitber├╝hmten Herrscher, die Aditja’s.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe golden-handed, soft-tongued Savit─Б is descending from heaven (to be present) thrice (daily) at the sacrifice; accept, Savit─Б, the praise (recited) by the worshippers, and thereupon grant to us all our desires.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Savitar of the golden hands and the lovely tongue, being master at the rite three times a dayтАФ
and (when), Savitar, you have set your signal-call among the gods, then impel wholeness to us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is either a syntactic fragment – a long NP in the nominative establishing the topic – or p├бtyam─Бnaс╕е is a predicated pres. part. (The published translation takes it as the former.) In c ca appears to be subordinating, given the accent on the verb ├б┼Ыreс╕е. I would now be inclined to delete the тАЬandтАЭ in the published translation and remove the parens.

from тАЬwhen.тАЭ

+Griffith

The fair-tongued Savitar, the golden-handed, comes thrice from heaven as Lord in our assembly.
Bear to the Gods this song of praise, and send us, then, Savitar, complete and perfect safety.

+Geldner

Savitri mit goldener Hand und sch├╢ner Zunge, der dreimal des Tages auf das Opfer ein Anrecht hat - Wenn du, Savitri, deinen Weckruf an die G├╢tter gerichtet hast, dann weise uns Vollz├дhligkeit zu!

+Grassmann

Dreimal des Tags nimmt Savitar am Fest theil, mit sch├╢ner Zunge und mit gold’nen H├дnden; O Savitar, zu G├╢ttern drang dein Preis hin, o schaff uns her die ganze Schar der G├╢tter.

+Wilson

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay (our) praises and prayers, the causes of good fortune, attain at this sacrifice Viс╣гс╣Зu, the object of many rites; he, the wide-stepping; whose commands the many-blending regions of space, the genitive rators (of all beings), do not disobey.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The recitations, the chants have gone to Viс╣гс╣Зu of many wonders as if on a journey of victorious BhagaтАФ
(Viс╣гс╣Зu) the wide-striding humped (bull), who has many (women). The young mothers-to-be are not neglectful.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I am not entirely certain why тАЬvictorious BhagaтАЭ is brought in here in a simile in this Viс╣гс╣Зu vs. I suppose that our praises are making a triumphal procession to Viс╣гс╣Зu, and the mention of Bhaga may suggest our hope that these praises will be met with a satisfactory portion of goods in return. See 21c below.

In cd it is tempting (see, e.g., Oldenberg) to make mardhanti the verb of the rel. cl.

beginning with y├бsya, which otherwise lacks a verb and appears truncated. But mardhanti is stubbornly unaccented. Construing y├бsya p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е as a relativized expression of possession, we can assume that it asserts that Viс╣гс╣Зu has a large female entourage; these females are further characterized in the independent clause in d as тАЬgeneratricesтАЭ (j├бnitr─лс╕е), for which тАЬmothers-to-beтАЭ seemed a more acceptable English rendering, who attend on him and do not neglect him. What this is all about escapes me, though Viс╣гс╣Зu is associated with the wives of the gods in I.156.2.

+Griffith

To Visnu rich in marvels, songs And praises shall go as singers on the road of Bhaga,-
The Chieftain of the Mighty Stride, whose Mothers, the many young Dames, never disregard him.

Zu Vishnu gehen die Loblieder, die Preisges├дnge zu dem Vielmeisternden wie bei der Fahrt eines siegreichen Gl├╝ckshelden. Er ist der weitschreitende Riese, dessen Gefolge viele Frauen sind. Nicht kommen die jungen Frauen, die Geb├дrerinnen zu kurz.

+Grassmann

Zum wunderstarken Vischnu gingen preisend die Lieder, jubelnd wie auf Gl├╝ckes Wegen; Der weithin schreitet, hoch, und dessen M├╝tter die jugendlichen, vielen, nimmer fehlen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, invested with all energies, has filled both heaven and earth with his greatness; do you, who are the destroyer of cities, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, the leader of a conquering host, collect cattle and bestow them abundantly upon us.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Indra, being master by virtue of all his heroic powers, filled both world-halves with his greatness,
stronghold-splitter, Vr╠еtra-smasher, possessor of a bold host. Having massed it together, bring to us here an abundance of livestock.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. construe the instr. v├н┼Ыvair v─лrya├мс╕е as the object of p├бtyam─Бnaс╕е (тАЬbeing master of all v─лry├б-), but when p├бtya- takes an object, it is in the acc., including once in this hymn: 8c patyate v├н┼Ыvam. In the only other passage in which Grassmann identifies the verb stem as taking an instr., VI.13.4, I take the instr. as here, as expressing the means by which the subject displays his mastery.

+Griffith

Indra, who rules through all his powers heroic, hath with his majesty filled earth and heaven.
Lord of brave hosts, Fort-crusher, Vrtra-slayer, gather thou up and bring us store of cattle.

+Geldner

Indra, der ├╝ber alle Manneskr├дfte gebeut, hat die beiden Welth├дlften mit seiner Gr├╢├Яe ausgef├╝llt, der Burgenzerst├╢rer, der Vritrat├╢ter mit k├╝hner Heerschar. Bring du uns zusammenraffend viel des Viehs her!

+Grassmann

Versehn mit allen Heldenkr├дften, Indra, durchdrang mit seiner Gr├╢sse beide Welten; Der Burgen bricht, den Vritra niederschmettert, zusammenraffend bring uns viele Heerden.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬN─Бsatyas, my protectors, inquirers (after the wishes) of your kinsman, beautiful is your cognate appellation of A┼Ыvins; be to us the liberal donors of riches; do you, who are irresistible, protect the offerer (of the oblation) with unblameable (defences).]тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The N─Бsatyas, asked about our kinship, are my fathers. Our cherished name is our common birth with the A┼Ыvins.
Because you are wealth-givers of wealth to us, you keep watch over giving with unstinting (gifts), as undeceivable ones.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half-vs. treats the kinship we share with the A┼Ыvins, a theme occasionally touched on elsewhere (e.g., VIII.73.12 adduced by Geldner). The grammatical problem in the hemistich is the (pseudo-)root noun cmpd. bandhupс╣Ы╠Бch-, which has been interpr. both actively (тАЬasking about [their] kinshipтАЭ: Grassmann, Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], L├╝ders 526, Scarlatta 328-29) and passively (тАЬasked about [their] kinshipтАЭ: Renou). I have followed the Renou path, on the assumption that it is more likely that humans are asking the A┼Ыvins about it than that the A┼Ыvins are wondering about it themselves. But in general I prefer root noun compounds to have active meaning, and it is possible that the majority position is the correct one. It does not seem to have too much effect on the interpr. of the rest.

+Griffith

My Sires are the Nasatyas, kind tokinsmen: the Asvins’ kinship is a glorious title.
For ye are they who give us store of riches: ye guard your gift uncheated by the bounteous.

+Geldner

Die Nasatya┬┤s sind meine V├дter, die sich nach ihren Angeh├╢rigen erkundigen. Die Verwandtschaft der Asvin ist ein sch├╢nes Wort. Ihr beide seid uns ja Geber von Reicht├╝mern, ihr erhaltet die Schenkung durch gleich vollkommene Gaben, wenn ihr nicht hintergangen werdet.

+Grassmann

Die biedern sind mir Aeltern, hold den Ihren, verwandt ist mir der Ritter theurer Name; Ihr seid ja uns der Sch├дtze Schatzverleiher; die Gabe sch├╝tzt ihr ungef├дhrdet, huldreich.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSages acquainted with the past, excellent is that beautiful appellation under which you have both become gods in (the sphere of) Indra; do you, Indra, the invoked of many, a friend, (associated) with the beloved с╣Ыbhus, shape this prayer for our benefit.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

That beautiful appellation: c─Бru n─Бma = agreeable or acceptable act or devotion, n─Бmakarma n─Бm─Бn─Бm v─Б, c─Бru, manoharam, by which the A┼Ыvins attained deification, yena devatvam pr─Бpnutha; in the preceding verse, saj─Бtyam c─Бru n─Бma is explained as saj─Бte bhavam kaman─лyam, desirable cognate appellation

+Jamison Brereton

Great is this cherished name of yours, o poets [=R╠еbhus], that you all become тАЬgodsтАЭ to Indra.
You are partner with the dear R╠еbhus, much-invoked one. (All of you,) fashion this insight here for us to win.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There is phraseological connection between the first p─Бda of this vs. and the previous vs.: c─Б╠Бru n─Б╠Бma тАЬdear nameтАЭ repeats verbatim the end of 16b, and though they are etymologically unrelated, kavayaс╕е in 17a echoes ├бkavaiс╕е in 16d.

The first half of the verse most likely refers to the с╣Ъbhus, though they are not named until c. The тАЬdear nameтАЭ of these unnamed subjects is probably тАЬgods,тАЭ the predicative voc. dev─Б(с╕е) in b. The с╣Ъbhus were not originally divine, but achieved the status of gods because of their wondrous acts in the sacrifice. So to be addressed as тАЬgodsтАЭ by Indra is precious to them indeed.

The second half-vs. consists of a p─Бda (c) with a sg. nom. (s├бkh─Б) referring to Indra, accompanied by a pl. instr. (с╣Ыbh├║bhiс╕е) and no verb, followed by one (d) with a 2nd pl. impv. (takс╣гat─Б). It is tempting to construe the two p─Бdas together, with a mixture of constructions: the sg. nom. + instr. serving as the equivalent of a pl. subj.

to the verb in d, but I have kept strictly to the grammar, as do the standard tr.

+Griffith

This is, ye Wise, your great and glorious title, that all ye Deities abide in Indra.
Friend, Much-invoked! art thou with thy dear Rbhus: fashion ye this our hymn for our advantage.

Das ist, o weise, euer theures Wesen, dass G├╢tter alle ihr bei Indra weilet, Vereint den lieben Ribhu’s, vielgerufen, macht unsre Bitte kr├дftig zum Erlangen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay Aryaman, Aditi, the adorable (gods), and the unimpeded functions of Varuс╣Зa (protect) us; keep us from (following) the course unpropitious to offspring, and may our dwelling be abundant in progeny and cattle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Keep us from the course: yuyota no anapaty─Бni gantoс╕е: anapaty─Бni = putr─Бс╣З─Бm ahit─Бni karmaс╣Зi tanm─Бrg─Бt pс╣Ыthak kuruta

+Jamison Brereton

Aryaman, Aditi, (all those) worthy of our sacrificeтАФthe
commandments of Varuс╣Зa cannot be cheatedтАФ
(all of you,) keep us from coming to childlessness. Let our course be full of offspring and livestock.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes pl. yaj├▒├нy─Бsaс╕е as predicated of aryam─Б╠БтАж ├бditiс╕е with p─Бda a simply a nominal clause; this is strictly impossible, since the predicate adj. should be dual. Geldner explains the plural on the grounds that the poet is thinking of the other ─Аdityas. This is possible, but I prefer to take yaj├▒├нy─Бsaс╕е as a third term referring to an unspecified set of other gods (quite possibly the rest of the ─Аdityas), and all three terms as the subj. of pl. yuy├│ta in c. (So also Renou) The naс╕е in p─Бda a then simply anticipates the same form in c, and b is parenthetical.

+Griffith

Aryaman, Aditi deserve our worship: the laws of Varuna remain unbroken.
The lot of childlessness remove ye from us, and let our course be rich in kine and offspring.

+Geldner

Aryaman, Aditi sind uns anbetungswert. Nicht zu hintergehen sind die Gebote des Varuna. Bewahret uns davor, in Kinderlosigkeit zu geraten. Unser Lebensweg sei kinderreich, reich an Vieh.

+Grassmann

Zu ehren sind uns Arjaman, Aditi, untr├╝glich sind des Varuna Gesetze, Entfernt von unserm Leben Kindermangel; an Kindern reich und Vieh sei unser Wandel.

+Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMay the messenger of the gods, engendered in many plural ces, everywhere proclaim us void of offence; may earth and heaven, the waters, the sun, and the vast firmament, with the constellation, hear us.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The messenger of the gods, impelled forth in many formsтАФlet him pronounce us blameless in our entirety.
Let Earth, Heaven, and the Waters hear us, and the Sun with the heavenly bodies, and the broad midspace.

+Griffith

May the Gods’ envoy, sent to many a quarter, proclaim us sinless for our perfect safety.
May Earth and Heaven, the Sun, the waters, hear us, and the wide firmament and constellations.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the (divine) showerers (of benefits), the deities of the mountains, and those abiding in fixed habitations, propitiated by the sacrificial food, hear us; may Aditi, with the ─Аdityas, heqar us; may the Maruts grant us auspicious felicity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abiding in fixed habitations: dhruvakс╣гem─Бsaс╕е ni┼Ыcalasth─Бnaс╕е, those of fixed plural ces; it may be an epithet of parvat─Бsaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

Let the bullish mountains with stable dwelling places hear us, as they become exhilarated on the refreshing drink.
Let Aditi with the ─Аdityas hear us. Let the Maruts extend to us beneficial shelter.

+Griffith

Hear us the mouatains which distil the rain-drops, and, resting firm, rejoice in freshening moisture.
May Aditi with the Adityas hear us, and Maruts grant us their auspicious shelter.

+Geldner

Es sollen uns die bullenhaften Berge erh├╢ren, die feststehenden, die sich an der Idaspende g├╝tlich tun. Mit den Aditya┬┤s soll uns Aditi erh├╢ren, die Marut sollen uns ihren gl├╝ckbringenden Schutz gew├дhren.

+Grassmann

Die starken Berge m├╢gen uns erh├╢ren, die festgegr├╝ndet sich des Trunks erfreuen; Es h├╢r’ uns Aditi mit ihren S├╢hnen, die Marutschar verleihe sichern Schutz uns.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay our path ever be easy of going, and provided with food; sprinkle, gods, the plural nts with sweet water; (safe) in your friendship, Agni, may my fortune never be impaired, but may I occupy a dwelling (abounding) with riches and ample food.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let our path be always easy to travel, abounding in food. Gods, saturate the plants with honey.
(Let there be) a share in your fellowship for me, Agni. You should not be neglectful. Might I reach the seat of wealth consisting in much
livestock.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take bh├бgaс╕е as the subj. of mс╣Ыdhy─Б(с╕е) in c; e.g., Geldner тАЬBhaga [das Gl├╝ck] m├╢ge in meiner Freundschaft nicht fehlen, o Agni.тАЭ With such a 3rd ps. subj., this requires mс╣Ыdhy─Бс╕е to be a precative (Renou calls it a тАЬpseudo-pr├йcatifтАЭ for some reason) rather than a straight 2nd sg. opt. This is, of course, not impossible.

But the desire expressed here, that Agni make sure that Bhaga does the right thing, does not seem the usual type of prayer addressed to gods in the RV. I take p─Бda c as consisting of two clauses, the first nominal, the 2nd, addressed to Agni, consisting only of a negative and a verb (cf. for this construction with this verb, n├б mardhanti in 14d above), with Agni the subj. I take bh├бgaс╕е as a common noun in the published translation; alternatively it might mean тАЬ(May) Bhaga (be) in partnership with me.тАЭ The final word of the vs., the gen. purukс╣г├│с╕е тАШconsisting in much livestockтАЩ, is a bahuvr─лhi variant of the phrase bh┼л╠Бri pa┼Ыv├бс╕е тАШabundance of livestockтАЩ, likewise ending its vs. in 15d.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬTaste (Agni) the oblations, make manifest (for us) abundant food measure out the viands before us; you overcome all those (who are) our enemies in conflict; favourably inclined towards us lighten up all our (ceremonies) day by day.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Sweeten our oblations, illuminate our refreshments entirely. Mete out full measures of fame in our direction.
Conquer all our rivals in combat, Agni. Through all the days, shine benevolently on us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Oldenberg is disturbed by t─Б╠Бm╠Рin c and suggests emending pс╣Ыts├║ t─Б╠Бm╠Рto pс╣Ыtsut─Б╠Б, loc. sg. of pс╣Ыtsut├н-. Because of the peculiar mid-p─Бda position of t─Б╠Бn, I favor this suggestion though it requires erasing one accent.

+Griffith

Enjoy the offering: beam thou strength upon us; combine thou for our good all kinds of glory.
Conquer in battle, Agni, all those foemen, and light us every day with loving kindness.

+Geldner

La├Я dir die Opfer schmecken, strahle Labsale aus, teil uns die Ehren zu! Besiege alle diese Feinde im Kampf, o Agni; alle Tage erstrahle uns wohlgesinnt!

+Grassmann

Geniess die Opfer, strahl herbei uns Nahrung und miss uns zu, o Agni, reiche Sch├дtze, Besiege alle Feinde in den Schlachten, und alle Tage leuchte wohlgesinnt uns.

+Elizarenkova
